< Review>
-Cash only -No tap list -Inexpensive -Very cold bottles of beer || The best dive bar I've gotten to know. I avoided 36/36 for a long time but, to my surprise, I find it clean, well ventilated, spacious, and accommodating. Two bar-sized pool tables, a decent jukebox selection, never too loud. Inexpensive. Downsides are a lack of taps for beer, no proper ginger ale for ginger-related drinks. But, no one expected it to be perfect. If you walk in at all, you're not really going to care about a few missing ingredients or components; in fact - one would argue - this adds to the aesthetic of the place. Trust me on this one; if you're willing to go at all, you're going to accidentally end up loving it. PROTIP: There's a laundromat right next door; do some laundry, play some pool, grab a drink.<//Review>

< review>
The manager of this shop gave me an important lesson on supporting local business and game shops like this and I can't help but think about it from time to time. I didn't leave that day buying something but I certainly came back within a week to make my purchase. It's been a couple years and I still havent had time to complete the set but I break it out and complete something from time to time to relax. Each time I do, I think about the manager who kind of gave me a lecture and how much I needed that. How much that kind of stuck with me and how it lead to the simple realization that supporting shops like these is the only way we not only get awesome stuff like this locally but we get an actual community to hang out and play with.

Thank you to that manager or employee or whoever it was but sometimes a lecture and time to think on it can really help to change someone for the better. Even if it's small.<//review>

< review>
My Nephew & Niece said this place is the BEST!

We stoped by today for the soft opening of La Michoaca Ice Cream and what a great business opening up in the area. For being a rainy day this place was jam packed, which only means one thing... Ice Cream must be Gooood!

As we waited in line we were welcomed and greeted by the awesome staff. Wait time was not bad considering it was a full house, they had the lines moving.

Our Order was:

-One Banana Split with your choice of ice cream and toppings. We chose 2 scoops of Oreo ice cream and one scoop of the fruity pebble ice cream along with traditional toppings (Chocolate syrup, whipped cream, & Cherries).

-One Single scoop of Oreo ice cream in a cup.

Both were really delicious, you could taste the quality of the ice cream. The amount per serving was very generous, they definitely don't hold back on that.
They have so many delicious options to choose from like Paletas (Ice Cream), Bionicos, Choco bananas, and so much more!

I seriously can't wait for the summer days to come around so I can be here daily getting a fresh drink of Agua Fresca!

Stop by and check them out, you won't be disappointed :)

Located in a plaza with tons of self parking.< /review>

<user_id>110223448783380710704<//user_id>< Review>
Riverbank has lots of big boulders.  Water is so clean. We saw so many little fish. Lots of shallow areas for families. We think this crossing is better than Bridgeport Crossings, which is more famous.  There is a short but level hike from parking to various river access points.  A bit of a climb down but very manageable even while carrying a toddler.

The unpaved parking lot is small. When we arrived at 9.30am on an Aug weekday, there were plenty of parking. In fact that's when some folks seem to be leaving, perhaps overnight campers. But by the time we left at 11.30am, the lot was full and cars were parked on the dusty road before the bridge where the No Parking signs are.  The last few miles is narrow, bumpy and unpaved. Drive slowly - 2 way traffic.</Review>

Best place around to go swimming. Its a short hike in to the best spots but it's worth it. Beaches are usually occupied by a few people but never feels too crowded. < Rate>
5<//Rate>
<review>This is the best spot  along the Yuba River  I've  been to so far  Here are a few tips I wish I knew before going.  Beware that you have to drive a few miles down an unpaved road to get there but its in fair condition...just a few big bumps to watch out for.  When you reach the Purdon bridge, take the trail that you see before you cross unless you like hiking through rugged terrain and poison oak.
I tried swimming in the quiet and gorgeous area right below the bridge but there were way too many creatures in the water.
You will know for sure you found THE spot along the trail when you see the rock formations and perfect pools of water.  The rapids are fun (and safe) to ride down also ...just remember to keep your butt up!
Just a heads up... i did see a rattle snake in the rocks we were climbing on near the water and a couple water snakes.
Worth the long drive for sure.</review><Pics>None<//Pics>< resp>
None< /resp>

< Text>
This place has a variety of Halva flavors.  So we go there for the Halva.  We stay to browse the other stuff, which runs the gamut from Eastern European to Middle Eastern.  The prices seem fair and the service is personable and helpful. Fortunately there is enough demand for their goods that they have been around for a while.  If I ever find a recipe that has something I can't find at Whole Foods or Berkeley Bowl and I *NEED* it, a trip to Crossroads never disappoints.  Pay them a visit.  Especially if you've never had Halva.<//Text>

I know it's difficult during this time, it's difficult for all of us but we hope to do our part to reduce the curve and what not.

Let me tell you right now, do you know how difficult it is to fine good hobby paints online for a decent price without the sellers milking your wallet dry? Exactly. There used to be a shop that I would always ALWAYS go to for my supplies : Hobby Co. San Francisco. That place had everything I needed but unfortunately they have since closed and it's difficult to acquire any sort of paint from any hobby shop that are still opened.

<Review>We had an hour or so of time to burn so I happen to see a new Gundam place opened up so we drove up to check it out. I am absolutely amazed by what the owners have done. Obviously a lot of thoughts has been put into setting up the store and they have done it so well.

Firstly, the place is new and clean. Upon entering there is a 1/10 Char's Zaku on display. Then there are a few tables where customers can use to build Gundams. A great place to hang out. They even have a paint room with proper ventilation and masks, all free for customers to use. That's an awesome idea, not only selling Gundam, but also help promote the building. There are some really experienced builders there who are making some nice looking build.

Then there is a place to hang out with a couch+TV showing, of course, Gundam episodes. Surround which are a glass showcase of some really nice builds. I was salivating just looking at the details and craftsmanship there.

The actual kits that are for sale is in another room. I wonder why they don't open up the place. Anyway, they have a great collection, aside from Bandai kits, which they mostly have PG/MG/RG and a little bit of recent HGs, they also have quite a few sets of Dragon Momoko kits, which are totally rare esp in the US. I was really tempted by the 1/35 Unicorn bust, it was hard to keep my wallet closed.

They have been opened for just a few months. The service is very friendly,  it is clear that the owners are huge Gundam fans and love to make more friends.

I am sure I will be back.. Hopefully that Unicorn will still be there when I clear out my backlogs at home.< /Review><Pics>None</Pics><Response>{'time': 1520898185743, 'text': 'Really a long review!\nThank you for taking your time.\nI am so glad you like our ideas.\nGunpla is freedom~~~hope to see u soon ~~~\n\nReally appreciate it!'}</Response>< GmapID>
